1445963968941</Time>
<rating>5</rating>< Review>
From what I've read, tire plugs typically cost $5 or less, so the fact Snyder's charges $10 isn't great, but things tend to be more expensive in the mountains and I'm still happy with their service.  They were overloaded and missing two mechanics today before a storm is due, but one of their mechanics was still willing to take the time to talk to me on the phone about fixing a screw in my tire.  He recommended the cheaper plug over a patch from the inside because plugs tend to last longer in our weather.  Plugs are quick to install so he had the first one done in a few minutes.  While I waited, I noticed another tire also had a screw in it!  I rolled my car and the mechanic checked each tire and we found a third tire had a much older beat up screw in it.  All the screws were only half an inch so I'm not sure any were actually causing leaks yet, although I'd noticed the pressure on two of the tires was abnormally low a week ago.  He charged me $20 instead of $30 for all three and it was done in about 10 minutes.  He also filled every tire with air to 40psi which he said is recommended on our curvy roads.

Also, I often find tire places will try to upsell you on things like getting an alignment or replacing your tires because the treads are worn but there were none of those shenanigans here.

UPDATE: I came back two years later to ask if I should worry about a cut in the sidewall of a tire about 1" long and 1/4" deep.  They inspected it and said nothing to worry about.  I'm pleased they didn't try to sell me repairs I didn't need.<//Review>

As soon as we walked in and quit gawking at how cool the place looked, we were greeted by a friendly ma√Ætre d‚Äô who set us up with a table. She was great! Probably couldn‚Äôt have been more friendly and welcoming‚Ä¶ she made us feel like we‚Äôd been there before and were being welcomed back. Thanks for the awesome service, Steph.

We tried the 2x4, which was excellent. Also gave the Cloudy 5000 a whirl, and a collab DIPA they did with brewery out of Nevada. I *think* it was called Mel-O-Vision. Regardless, you better get in there before it‚Äôs all gone because it was TASTY!! Hubert rounded our thirst. So. Good.

We also gave the pork gyoza (perfect, slightly crispy and hot), kobe corndogs, sprouts (mmm, savory!), sticky wings (I think it was a whole chicken. Huge pieces!), and yellow curry a try. We inhaled all of them and there were still items on the menu we didn‚Äôt get to that looked incredible. Neat mix of Asian-inspired step-up-from bar food.

The wall murals and particularly, a whole bunch of nun-chucks hanging from the ceiling were pretty eye-appealing. Great music and old school kung-fu movies on the tv‚Äôs. Our San Clemente friends will be back soon, and I‚Äôm jealous.< /Text>

< text>
A downtown micro brewery.

I'm not a drinker so I can't weigh in on the beer but the food is pretty good.

Basil fried rice is awesome (add that egg!)

The flat breads are decent single thin crust pizzas. Perfect for one or even split for 2. (Dynamite Seoul)

The handcut fries are amazing and we always get extra ketchup like white trash redneck stereotypes because it's that good.

A typical order from us is:

Tatoyaki, Handcut Fries extra ketchup, Thai me up add egg and one of the three flat breads.

They've been open for a couple months now and we make an effort to eat there once a paycheck because it's fast delicious food. For what you pay, you get it. We get take out and it takes 15 minutes.

They also play 90's oldschool hip hop like wutang and nwa while appreciating old school martial art films that inspired the RZA and Method and the ODB.

I'd like to see them open for lunches eventually. They'll probably do real well this summer (2019)< /text>

< review>
This is a fun place in a great part of LA. spending $100 feels more like spending $200 it is reasonably priced, but feels more wealthy than it is. I Did not eat here, so cannot comment on the food, I will say the dishes smelled and looks delicious and portion size was fair with a nice selection of Italian Classics and California cuisine. Nice wine list,and great cocktails. Please try the Mediterranean mule, or the basil martini both of which are delicious on a summer day. All in all a great place to take family to old young and in between after a visit to the museums or the concert.< /review>

The restaurant has a wonderful bar area with a modern design. It's in a nice Central spot close to the Disney Music Hall and the Dorothy Chandler Pavilion offering valet parking.

The food was good with classic homemade pasta  and a little twist such as spaghetti with sardines in a nice olive oil sauce & beef tenderloin and potatoes.

The best part is they have a huge selection of pastries and breads in the back of the restaurant that you can take home with you or enjoy on the outside Terrace.

So no matter if you're just getting off work in your suit or spending a day casual with jeans and a t-shirt you'll find this restaurant has something for everyone.<//Text>

< Review>
If you have a group coming here for lunch or dinner, ask about the room in the back which has an option to close off for privacy.
We enjoyed a family style service, while meeting with the staff of the Meg Quigley Vivaldi Competition and Bassoon Symposium.
Very elegant experience, delicious food, great house wine selection and all served with care and a smile.
It is pricey, yet it is located near the Disney Concert Hall and across from the MOCA. You may valet park or take advantage of the various parking lots in the area. Street parking is about $5 an hour.< /Review>

<date>1444529940437</date><UserId.>102532010049364567402</UserId.><Name>Theresa Menard</Name>< review>
I was not impressed . Service was very slow and scattered. We had a reservation and arrived on time but no table was awaiting us. We were offered two bad locations - behind bar, handicapped or by kitchen and then the maitre'd ' tried to give them away to walk-ins. We ended up on the patio where the ceiling fans barely worked and it was 88 degrees. The hostess did not want to seat us at a 4-person table - I repeat, we had a reservation!  I ordered the artichoke salad and the waiter told me they were out of the carpaccio that came with it . There was nothing similar on the menu so I asked for just an artichoke with arugula salad ( the menu description minus the carpaccio) but never received anything (the waiter forgot?) and when I inquired, was told they were out of artichokes. My scallop appetizer was raw and very, very, very greasy. My husbands pappardelle was, unbelievably, so overcookef that it was a glutinous mass and his buffala mozzarella salad had no dressing. No one ever offered parmesano or olive oil . My glass of wine eventually showed up; eventually the waiter asked about dessert; eventually my espresso showed up. How the heck do you ruin an Italian meal??  When they cleared the table, the bus person left a large spinach leaf from the salad sitting there. All in all . Very poor service and substandard food. Not worth your time.</review>
